{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Go Mummy - 9-Aug 2020 [devlog/go-mummy]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/IDptS0CU1ug/2020-08-09","description":"<p>The last series of work has been play testing, trying to catalogue and fix bugs and adding polish the game where possible.</p>\n<p>I've been wanting to bring a bit more visual interest to the screens I had though I'm limited in the game itself, the main options screen could do with some love.</p>\n<p>The screen initially I'd picked <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jVhlJNJopOQ\">Papyrus</a>, albeit at random for it's oldworldly feel and the screen looked like this:</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-20b.png\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p>But I wanted something that harked back a little to the original game roots and give it a bit of an egyptian feel (or certainly what I imagine that would feel like).</p>\n<p>I ran through a number iterations until I found a font and some border images that started to bring it together:</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-08-09.png\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p>The first was a little too <em>streetwise</em> and the second looked like it would suit a shooting game of some sort. I liked the third, but the fourth felt a little more dynamic which is how I think of the game - a bit frantic.</p>\n<p>To get this to load into NextBASIC, I have three options:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>I can export as an 8-bit BMP and load on the machine using <code>.bmpload</code> - which is probably fine, but has a little more latency that I'd like.</li>\n<li>I can convert the file first to an BMP and then to <a href=\"https://wiki.specnext.dev/File_Formats\">an SL2 file</a> - which is a pure dump of the screen layer. Then easily loaded back in using <code>LAYER 2,1: LOAD &#34;screen.sl2&#34; LAYER</code>. This is quick (there's no calculation to be done as it represents a memory dump) but it does read of the SD card. This would be fine if I was showing this screen once, but I show it many times, particularly through the option screens.</li>\n<li>Generate the SL2 file, and load individual thirds into banks - this is the method I used since the data is loaded in memory for quick copying back into the screen memory.</li>\n</ol>\n<p>I made <a href=\"https://zx.remysharp.com/tools/\">another online tool</a> that lets me upload any file format, and so long as it's 256x192 (or not wider than 256) then my code will translate the data to both an 8-bit BMP (with the default Spectrum Next palette) <em>and</em> an SL2 file (which is very similar to a BMP, just ordered slightly differently).</p>\n<p>Once I have the SL2 file, I need to break it into 3 equal parts of 16K (the size of a memory bank) and for the final touch, the last third of the screen is solid black for 16 lines - which I can do at the same time.</p>\n<p>A unix tool called <code>dd</code> can be used to split the file up:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">$ dd if=screen.sl2 of=screen1.bin bs=16k count=1 skip=0\n$ dd if=screen.sl2 of=screen2.bin bs=16k count=1 skip=1\n$ dd if=screen.sl2 of=screen3.bin bs=16k count=1 skip=2\n</code></pre>\n<p>This will create 3 files of 16K blocks each (based on screen.sl2).</p>\n<p>The final task is to block out the last 16 lines in black pixels - <code>0x00</code> which conveniently is what comes out of <code>/dev/zero</code>, so I can source that stream and use <code>dd</code> to write it into the <code>screen3.bin</code> file:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">$ dd if=/dev/zero bs=4k count=1 oseek=3 of=screen3.bin\n</code></pre>\n<p>Now the binary files can be reploaded into banks then loaded into the LAYER on demand:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token keyword\">LOAD</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"screen1.bin\"</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">20</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">LOAD</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"screen2.bin\"</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">21</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">LOAD</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"screen3.bin\"</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">22</span>\n<span class=\"token comment\">; later in the code</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">20</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">COPY</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">TO</span> <span class=\"token number\">9</span>   <span class=\"token comment\">; bank 9 is the start of LAYER 2</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">21</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">COPY</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">TO</span> <span class=\"token number\">10</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">22</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">COPY</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">TO</span> <span class=\"token number\">11</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>So the state of play on Sunday 9 August is that all the (known) bugs are fixed, the new music and sound effects are in place, high scores are updating and saving. I'm investigating a couple of performance tweaks (that aren't required, but will be nice if I can it off) which leaves me with one last problem to solve.</p>\n<p>Do I keep the name <em>&#34;Oh Mummy!&#34;</em>? There's other clones of Amsoft's Oh Mummy, some have a different name, some reuse the name, but there is a question over copyright. I'd hope that copyright holders would see this as a hat-tip to old but it bears considering.</p>\n<p>So, so far there's some ideas:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Mummy Mummy!</li>\n<li>Return of Oh Mummy!</li>\n<li>Oh Daddy!</li>\n<li>Go Mummy!</li>\n<li>(and) Oh Remmmy!</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Although the last one is rather self serving, I quite like it - just trying to work out how it fits in the story lineâ€¦ (I also prefer titles that are approximately the same length as the original).</p>\n<p>So closeâ€¦</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a vacation from twitter a fortnight ago and today I dipped my toe in only to be sucked into the void that's known as reality these days.</p>\n<p>I sincerely doubt I'll forget this time but I wanted to write all the same.</p>\n<p><strong>A quick precursor: this post includes bad language and serious topics, so, my kids in particular, please don't read this, come talk to us.</strong></p>\n<p>A quick look around and this is where we're at:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>We have a conservative government that's blindly lead us out of the EU (which we don't want)</li>\n<li>A government led by a person who skipped out on meetings to prepare us for a potential pandemic</li>\n<li>A pandemic</li>\n<li>A fucking pandemic, like, in those computer games where the world goes to shit and people start eating each other, but <strong>in reality</strong> and people aren't eating each other, but instead they're dying</li>\n<li>In the UK we've been under lockdown for the last 11 weeks</li>\n<li>I'm getting tubby (again), it's my forking DNA, it loves preserving fat cell in case global warming dumps us in a deeply cold climate (which frankly is entirely possible)</li>\n<li>I've put my shoes on twice in 11 weeks</li>\n<li>US Police brutality against black and people of colour has triggered nationwide (and actually worldwide) unrest and protest - in fact, &#34;Police brutality&#34; is just a clever avoidance of the fact that the police are murdering black folk. It's disgusting. It's unforgivable. It's deep, deep, racism that's ever present andâ€¦ andâ€¦ I've no fucking wordsâ€¦</li>\n<li>Women are treated like shit, still, decades after the women right's movements (that said, we still have huge problems with racism so it's hardly surprising)</li>\n<li>I don't know how adults aren't incredibly sad or incredibly angry <strong>all the fucking time</strong> - I know that if I scratch under the rather thin surface that's what's sitting there for me.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>I've seen a few posts of &#34;what a week&#34;, but this isn't just one week. &#34;This week&#34; is the culmination of decades and decades and centuries of persecution. Persecution towards anyone who didn't look, let's be honest, like a white man.</p>\n<p>I wouldn't ever call myself racist, but I know, when I examine closely that I've been racist. I wouldn't call myself sexist, but, again, I know I have been. I have been because it never occurred to me, because I've never been in that situation. That in itself is mind bogglingly fucked up. I get a free pass in life by total fluke.</p>\n<p>I'm a white guy, born in britain, middle-class enough, working in tech, with privilege left right and centre. <em>I am</em> the problem, <strong>it's on us</strong> (not the pandemic, but frankly it seems like the pandemic is just the planet's way of telling us something's a little more than fucked).</p>\n<p>I do have personal and professional ways that I can help make positive change, but good lord it feels like a piddle in the ocean.</p>\n<p>So, this week, people protest on the streets for equality, to be treated fairly and not in fear - becauseâ€¦human rights, right? This week we sit in our homes, not visiting friends, not getting hair cuts, not doing anything unless vital and we wait to hear that the pandemic is on the decline.</p>\n<p>More importantly, to me, this week, we talked (again) to our (white) kids to about racism, about sexism, about hate and fear. That, so far this week, is the best I've managed.</p>\n<p>I hope this time ends. I hope we return to a new normality. One where racism and sexism is thrown out in the open and ridiculed for the shameful attitude that it is. I hope those people in power suddenly wake up better people, not driven by their own selfish money and power hungry needs.</p>\n<p>But until then, I just wanted to remember: <a and &#34;-&#34;, so I'm using CSS to change visual state:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\"><span class=\"token selector\">.bool input:checked + label.t::before</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">content</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> <span class=\"token string\">'T'</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\n<span class=\"token selector\">.bool input + label::before</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">content</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> <span class=\"token string\">'-'</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">width</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> 100%<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">font-size</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> inherit<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">line-height</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> inherit<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>The problem was that when I tabbed focus to the checkbox, the label text didn't look focused. I could add a border (or something) to the label, but I wanted it to look the same as the browser default focus ring.</p>\n<p>TIL: Firefox has a <code>Highlight</code> that compliments webkit's focus ring colour, and (thankfully) Firefox ignores the <code>-webkit-</code> prefixed colour:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\"><span class=\"token selector\">.bool input:focus + label::before</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">outline</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> 5px auto Highlight<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token property\">outline</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> 5px auto -webkit-focus-ring-color<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Now it looks right:</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/til/focus-rings.png\" alt=\"TIL: focus rings\"></p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Go Mummy - 20-Jul 2020 [devlog/go-mummy]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/m1AyCAHasXA/2020-07-20","description":"<p>This week's episode: <em>Experiments in soundâ€¦or rather: failures in sound.</em></p>\n<p>Since I'm writing this game in NextBASIC I'm abstracted much higher up that machine code (which has it's obvious benefit to my programming experience). The downside is control over the machine.</p>\n<p>Currently <em>Oh Mummy</em> has (really cool) music thanks to Richard Faulkner (from the Spectrum Next facebook forum). To play sound effects poses a number of problems, and ultimately I've had to park the idea entirely.</p>\n<p>Since my game is pretty high speed and involves constant movement, any sound effect is going to have to run along side the rendering. The way BASIC is wired up doesn't really allow this. When I'm calling the <code>BEEP</code> function (for instance) I can't be moving my sprite.</p>\n<p>In machine code it doesn't work like this anyway, so it's useful to think in machine code context. The way it works at the lowest level is that the user code changes the interrupt routine (in web language this would be akin to request animation frame) and then tones would be adjusted at this point.</p>\n<p>Without knowing the details, I'm fairly confident that this is how the audio <code>DRIVER</code> call works to play the <a href=\"http://nextdaw.biasillo.com/\">NextDAW</a> music.</p>\n<p>So the <code>BEEP</code> function is pretty much out of the window. Not only because it'll pause the runtime enough to make playing uncomfortable, but also I can't design a beeper based sound to sound decent enough. Though it might be worth my looking at <a href=\"http://freestuff.grok.co.uk/beepola/\">Beepola</a>.</p>\n<p>NextBASIC also comes with a powerful <code>PLAY</code> function which sends commands to the AY-8-3912 chips. This does sound great (assuming I can construct the right string to send to the <code>PLAY</code> command) but it <em>also</em> suffers from locking up the play back.</p>\n<p>I also looked at <a href=\"https://shiru.untergrund.net/software.shtml\">Beepfx</a> which is Windows specific but does generate machine code that I can call from BASIC using <code>RANDOMIZE USR 60000</code>. This works pretty well for sounds and includes a very useful demo library of sound effects. The problem is that a) it also locks up until complete - which could be mitigated with extremely short sounds, but most importantly b) it's configured to run on a 3.5Mhz spectrum <em>not</em> one running at 28Mhz which is the speed I'm using to get the game to feel quick and responsive. The beepfx sounds are more like a crazed mouse on acid.</p>\n<p>Sadly, I can't get my head around the sound engineering maths required to modify the beepfx values, and switching down to 3.5Mhz, calling the routine, then speeding back up to 28Mhz has the same (if not worse) slow down.</p>\n<p>One novel approach that Dave Clarke (also of Spectrum Next facebook forum) uses is to enable the AY chips via the <code>OUT</code> function in BASIC, set the volume to zero, then adjust the volume on demand in his game loop. The same technique can be used to adjust the tones on demand to create effects.</p>\n<p>I also <a href=\"https://gist.github.com/remy/8dd68e03adfa023e9adf6c3c9dbee238\">experimented</a> with working through a string of toggles during the game loop and it kinda half works but the sounds I'm making are quite terrible <strong>and</strong> I'm competing with the background music for the AY chips (which in reality just doesn't let me play back).</p>\n<p>So, for the time being, this game will have to be sans sound effect. Which is a bit of shame. I think the only reasonable solution will be some machine code that hooks the interrupt and checks a queue for sound effects to play, but I've had limited success with the <a href=\"https://speccy.xyz/opcodes/im/\"><code>im 2</code> opcode</a>.</p>\n<p>That said, I did a bit of graphics tinkering and a small change is looking really nice now.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-20c.png\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/go-mummy/2020-07-20\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=m1AyCAHasXA:R2fOVqqAiIo:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-20c.png","linkMd5":"36a6017a7566625b8c083e81dc196496","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn100@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-36-951_ce46b629be096585.webp","destWidth":1584,"destHeight":1188,"sourceBytes":9705,"destBytes":47318,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-20c.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn100@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-36-951_ce46b629be096585.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=m1AyCAHasXA:R2fOVqqAiIo:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn59@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-57-313_0463cbea10b5b015.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/m1AyCAHasXA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn80@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-57-338_44b1e40ac9ba0eee.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476249},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"No undefsafe [til/javascript]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/gZKJghylBp8/no-undefsafe","description":"\n<p>I wrote a small JavaScript library called <a href=\"https://www.npmjs.com/package/undefsafe\">undefsafe</a> which I use in my work. I believe the <a href=\"https://lodash.com/docs/4.17.15#get\">_.get</a> lodash package is very similar (though I added a few super powers to my own library).</p>\n<p>However, with frameworks like <a href=\"https://nextjs.org/\">Next.js</a> and <a href=\"https://nuxtjs.org/\">Nuxt.js</a> (and likely others), I've found that I don't need undefsafe due to the <em>optional chaining</em> and <em>nullish coalescing</em> features that are provided with ES2020 (which are polyfilled for us in these frameworks).</p>\n<p>This means my code can go from this:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token keyword\">let</span> v <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token function\">undefsafe</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token keyword\">this</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token string\">'pkg.services.vulns.count'</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token operator\">||</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"not available\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>To this:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token keyword\">let</span> v <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">this</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>pkg<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>services<span class=\"token operator\">?.</span>vulns<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>count <span class=\"token operator\">??</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"not available\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>The nullish coalesce is useful because of <code>.count</code> is <code>0</code>, then the value of <code>v</code> is, correctly, zero.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til/javascript/no-undefsafe\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 11:15:40 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=gZKJghylBp8:gnAnrSr1u6M:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"8d473432fa23c2424978099297b9bcd3","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-400_631a4043e6866b36.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=gZKJghylBp8:gnAnrSr1u6M:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-400_631a4043e6866b36.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/gZKJghylBp8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn99@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-57-312_898b4be9f06d074b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476257},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Gotcha: Reading shorts [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/_lIRPF7quY0/gotcha-reading-shorts","description":"\n<p>Just in case you came here to find out what kind of shorts you need to wear for the best reading experience, I'll tell you up front: you'll be disappointed. A <a href=\"https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)#Common_integral_data_types\">short is a 16 bit integer</a>. Though I think this is just as interesting!</p>\n<p>Recently I had a requirement to read a file that contained an array of 16bit values. This means <em>pairs of bytes</em>. When we read files in the browser or in Node we get byte (8bit) and the process <em>should</em> be straight forward to view this data as 16bit data, but, as you might guess, it's not.</p>\n<h2>On the web</h2>\n<p>The web makes it mostly straight forward so long as you're working with files arranged in the same endianness as your own system.</p>\n<p>I want to write about endianness (mostly for my own understanding and recollection), but in lieu of that, MDN have a <a href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/Endianness\">good article on endianness</a> (TL;DR: defines the byte order, little being the bytes are reversed, which is also the most common format).</p>\n<p>To get a 16bit array out of a file, the process is relatively straight forward:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token comment\">// assuming result is an arrayBuffer, possibly from readAsArrayBuffer</span>\n<span class=\"token comment\">// [1, 2, ...]</span>\nresult<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>byteLength <span class=\"token comment\">// ? 512</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> data <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">Uint16Array</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>result<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\ndata<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>length <span class=\"token comment\">// ? 256 elements - correct (2 bytes per value)</span>\ndata<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span> <span class=\"token comment\">// ? first value is 513 (0x0201)</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>However, if your machine is little endian and your file is big endian (not super likely, but still), there's no straight forward way of getting this data so it needs a helping hand:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token comment\">// result is an arrayBuffer - as above</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> view <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">DataView</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>result<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> data <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">Uint16Array</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>result<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>byteLength<span class=\"token operator\">/</span><span class=\"token number\">2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">for</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token keyword\">let</span> i <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> i <span class=\"token operator\">&#60;</span> data<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>length<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> i<span class=\"token operator\">++</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  data<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>i<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> view<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">getUint16</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>i <span class=\"token operator\">*</span> <span class=\"token number\">2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token boolean\">false</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> <span class=\"token comment\">// false = read as big endian</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\ndata<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span> <span class=\"token comment\">// ? first value is now 258 (0x0102)</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Though, I still find it odd that the system defaults to little endian and yet <code>getUint16</code> defaults to big endian (if the <code>false</code> boolean is omitted).</p>\n<p>Node is a bit more of a struggle.</p>\n<h2>Inside node</h2>\n<p>When reading a file in Node using the <code>fs</code> module, either <code>readFile</code> or <code>readFileSync</code> you'll get a Node specific <code>Buffer</code> back. It extends the <code>ArrayBuffer</code> so you can get to the underlying buffer but you can't throw it into a new 16bit array - you need to use some careful code.</p>\n<p>I don't fully understand the inner workings, but when you do a <code>readFile</code> there's a <code>poolSize</code> property that changes has the data sits in the buffer. From the <a href=\"https://nodejs.org/dist/latest-v14.x/docs/api/buffer.html#buffer_buf_byteoffset\">docs</a>:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>â€¦when allocating a buffer smaller than Buffer.poolSize, the buffer doesn't start from a zero offset on the underlying ArrayBuffer.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>To see this in action, I can read a file and throw the buffer into a <code>Uint16Array</code> and see how wrong it is:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token comment\">// result is a Buffer object, which contains the same data arrangement</span>\n<span class=\"token comment\">// as our earlier example: [1, 2, ...] an a length of 512 bytes</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> bad <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">Uint16Array</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>file<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>buffer<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\nbad<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>length <span class=\"token comment\">// ? 4096 - ðŸ˜±wat</span>\nbad<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span> <span class=\"token comment\">// ? 8827 (and changes each time I run the code)</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Clearly not good. This is because there's junk bytes on our buffer, and so we need to makes sure we pick out the data correctly:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> good <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">Uint16Array</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>file<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>buffer<span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> file<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>byteOffset<span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> file<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>length <span class=\"token operator\">/</span> <span class=\"token number\">2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\ngood<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>length <span class=\"token comment\">// ? 256 ðŸ‘�</span>\ngood<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span> <span class=\"token comment\">// ? 513 ðŸ‘�</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Node has a <a href=\"https://nodejs.org/dist/latest-v14.x/docs/api/buffer.html#buffer_buf_swap16\">convenience method for swapping</a> the endianness of the bytes: <code>swap16</code>. Calling this method before loading the buffer into the <code>Uint16Array</code> will change the data from little endian (in my current case) to big endian.</p>\n<p>So that's how to get 16bit data.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2020/07/08/gotcha-reading-shorts\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=_lIRPF7quY0:rtGOET53Ack:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=_lIRPF7quY0:rtGOET53Ack:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/_lIRPF7quY0\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 08 Jul 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=_lIRPF7quY0:rtGOET53Ack:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"9ae59366d921275e9c6fa0908988af53","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn23@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-36-554_7824d0a523479e4d.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=_lIRPF7quY0:rtGOET53Ack:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn23@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-36-554_7824d0a523479e4d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/_lIRPF7quY0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn52@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-57-310_35c85f0dcd442dd2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476251},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Safari 10 supports module, but not nomodule [til/javascript]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/xf1IgAw3pZc/safari-10-supports-module-but-not-nomodule","description":"\n<p>More and more of my own project uses <code>&#60;script type=&#34;module&#34; Already a lot more shouting than anyone would want. It's been an exceedingly hot few days which also means no one is sleeping well. It all mounts up. Sometimes this blog is for me, and this is one of those times. This is unedited and raw.</p>\n<p><em>Content warning: stillbirth</em></p>\n<p>This morning I'm trying to work on a client project, some stupid data wrangling and I can't concentrate. The kids are asking me questions that I'd normally be happy to help, but instead I'm getting more frustrated and angry at myself. I can't solve this computing problem and I'm making repetitive mistakes.</p>\n<p>And then there's the lockdown since late March. In those 4 months, I've seen two friends. I've not been the gym (though it reopened a couple of weeks ago). I've outgrown my medium t-shirts and am now filling, once again, my large t-shirts. Julie, my partner, to say has her hands are full is an understatement. She has all the same pressures I have except that her full time job is our kids (during this lockdown), and being a full time parent is ten-fold more demanding that some stupid data wrangling. That's to say, in the scheme of things I don't really have anything to complain about. But I do. And I don't really have anyone to talk to.</p>\n<p>I can feel my chest is tight. I'm struggling to concentrate. It's not just all the crap we're dealing with. My body remembers. My body remembers that it would be Tia's tenth birthday this month. In a matter of weeks. It's like a foot that stands on my chest, just enough to make my breathing hard.</p>\n<p>Ten years today, I remember driving down the road (just around the corner where we live now) and I remember thinking at the time, this is level 10, we're right on 9 months and baby is coming real soon. This the level 10 boss and I need to drive carefully and play through this level carefully and not do anything unsafe because we're nearly there. We're nearly at the day that we meet our first child.</p>\n<p>Tia died during birth. Stillbirth. Though I don't like to say &#34;stillbirth&#34; because some people confuse stillbirth with miscarriages. It's not simple (both ways). We know that Tia was alive the week she was due. We think, as much as it hurts to think, that she kicked the day before we went into hospital. But she had died. We don't know why. I didn't and don't want to know why. I never wanted anyone or anything to blame. If there was something to blame then it might have been preventable and that path of madness is too much for me.</p>\n<p>After she was born, the days and weeks that followed I saw Tia in another universe. In a universe where Julie, myself and our newborn Tia were happy. Going for walks in the new pram, enjoying the sunshine and happiness. I'm not religious but wondered if I could have the chance to see Tia again after I died. It's something I ran over my mind over and over, something I needed to solve. I didn't believe in heaven and the variables involved was too much (was <em>everyone</em> in heavenâ€¦ etc) but I could see the appeal of Belief.</p>\n<p>I don't think about that anymore. Not all these years later. When she was born it was like our snow globe of a world had been thoroughly shaken - everything was unrecognisable. It took a long, long time for it to settle. Time doesn't heal, it changes you. Tia's loss is part of me, it's part of our family. I carry the pain as matter of fact. In the first year I feared that if I stopped hurting I wouldn't remember her and that I'd lose her. The pain is still there, the hole in my life is still there, it's just I carry it now. It's there: the hole of her not being in our daytime lives is part of me.</p>\n<p>And I need to cry, but I can't. Though this could be the anti-depressants I've been on for the last 4 years or so (please don't send unsolicited opinions on this). The the drugs help me in ways that I can't describe (they're not for Tia, they're for something else), but they do seem to put a plug on my ability to cry. I'm unsure whether it would make any difference, but that foot on my chest and that need to cry is like something on the edge of my vision that I can never quite focus properly on.</p>\n<p>I've got some time off around her birthday. The hope is that I'm able to disconnect myself enough to stop. To stop properly and to let the memories and emotions wash over me. This writing helps. It helps to know that friends see me and know about Tia. For her 10th birthday - a word that will never sit right but we don't have other words - we're having her gravestone cleaned. It's made of sandstone, enclosing a mix of heather plants, small stones, butterfly trinkets and a number of small soft toys. The headstone is heart shaped with the inscription:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>Tia Sharp</p>\n<p>31 August 2010</p>\n<p>Our heartbreaker.</p>\n<p>Our sleeping beauty.</p>\n<p>We will always love you.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2020/08/13/ten\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=RRE0jf9m52U:eaGZ9stybJ0:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=RRE0jf9m52U:eaGZ9stybJ0:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/RRE0jf9m52U\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 13 Aug 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=RRE0jf9m52U:eaGZ9stybJ0:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"a6998f0d64547eccf778088335c34142","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn50@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-36-399_0eeb830483d5bdc1.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=RRE0jf9m52U:eaGZ9stybJ0:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn50@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-36-399_0eeb830483d5bdc1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/RRE0jf9m52U":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn35@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-57-379_aa3fc7f2431cc181.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476247},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Clearing twitter [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/PGWWbobs69I/clearing-twitter","description":"\n<p>It's no surprise that twitter and similar sink holes are constantly trying to &#34;engage&#34; you so you can be sucked into their void. As someone who believes that the web belongs to its users and I browse the way <em>I want</em> I frequently change and block content on these sites so I can use them the way I would like.</p>\n<p>So here's a quick share on how I'm doing that.</p>\n<p>This is a simple example of how <em>I think</em> twitter can be improved - the picture below shows, highlighted in red, the &#34;trending news&#34; which really isn't news - or at least not news that I would recommend consuming. I certainly don't want to get my COVID-19 advice from the latest trending bullshit. More recently they have launched (possibly in split tests) a DM â€¦ &#34;thing&#34;? so I can use that to message people instead ofâ€¦what, email? WhatsApp? Not sure. Anyway, it's shit that I don't need in my life, so it's getting ejected.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/clean-twitter.png\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p>Step 1: get yourself <a href=\"https://github.com/gorhill/uBlock/\">uBlock Origin</a> (the origin bit is important) available for <a href=\"https://github.com/gorhill/uBlock/#installation\">most browsers</a></p>\n<p>Step 2: use the right click - block element picker to stop content from bothering you</p>\n<p>When you fire up the picker, you'll notice that Twitter (and other sites that don't believe in writing actual CSS classes) are using something to generate their CSS, which makes picking element using CSS selectors tricky.</p>\n<p>Except, the trick is to look for aria roles or even data properties. As much as I dislike these big companies, they <em>do</em> try to support a broad range of users via good use of accessibility and we can use that to our advantage.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/picking.png\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p>The uBlock Origin element picker will need a selector like <code>##div[aria-label=&#34;Timeline: Trending now&#34;]</code>, I'm not sure what the double hash is about, but it works.</p>\n<p>So now we can surf web pages the way <em>we want</em>.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a development I've been using <a href=\"http://cspect.org/\">Cspect</a> and for certain bits like yesterday's Fisher-Yates shuffle, I'll use <code>% RND</code> to get random numbers.</p>\n<p>However, I also want to prevent my game from being repeatable so I use <code>RANDOMIZE</code> as a standalone call which is supposed randomly seed the random functions:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>RANDOMIZE on its own (and RANDOMIZE 0 has the same effect) is different, because it really does randomise RND and % RND</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>And with any basic understanding of random numbers, they have to be seeded from something in the real world, so <em>time</em> is used:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>RANDOMIZE uses the time since the computer was switched on. Since this has gone up by the same amount each time RANDOMIZE is executed, the next % RND does more or less the same. You would get better randomness by replacing GO TO 10 by GO TO 20.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>â€¦and of course, when Cspect launches into my code to immediately run it, the time is <em>exactly the same</em> on each start up, so the seed, is also exactly the same! ðŸ¤¦</p>\n<hr>\n<p>I've been avoiding the details of gameplay until I got some of the core basics working - specifically the status of the tombs and when they were open or not.</p>\n<p>But now I've got that working, I decided to revisit the game and <a href=\"https://archive.org/details/Oh_Mummy_1984_Amsoft\">play it</a> looking at how the mummy's behaviour works.</p>\n<p>A few observations that I'll need to add:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Mummy's can't walk past each other (currently mine can slide under each other)</li>\n<li>The level difficulty applies to the AI in the mummy - current mine are turning entirely random. I suspect if I want to add AI, I'll need to decrease the random effect as difficulty increases</li>\n<li>Mummy's revealed in a tomb follow you to the next level, and if you don't lose a life from a mummy (or kill a mummy using a scroll), the in game mummy number increases quickly, so the game needs to work with 5+ mummy's in play (currently adding mummy's has a direct impact on game speed)</li>\n</ol>\n<p>I've also been reviewing how I'll unveil the tombs. extremely wary of runtime performance and have spent pretty much all my time sweating the details on game play without moving onto things like scoring, or the help screens etc.</p>\n<p>My last entry I continuously (which prints the sprite to screen) to using <code>SPRITE CONTINUE</code> which lets the hardware animate between points - in my case, the crossroads in the game.</p>\n<p>The video below shows before and after (around the 15 second mark). Before, the game play is sluggish as I hit around 4 mummy's and becomes unplayable after that. After, I'm easily able to get to 11 mummy's and they're still running around at breakneck speed!</p>\n<iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/v-wAs0-hZTo\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n<p>Next I want to work on the controls. I've noticed that when I play, sometimes I get stuck trying to turn a corner and the player just sits trying to move when they can't.</p>\n<p>So my idea to solve this is: if the player tries to move left before they're able to, continue them moving in the direction they were going before. i.e. if they were going up, and try to move left but hit a wall, keep going up (which is usually just one tick) then the left movement will kick in.</p>\n<p>The trick, I think, will be ensuring that this method can only occur during movement and not as the first movementâ€¦whatever that's supposed to mean.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/go-mummy/2020-06-07\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=4ZEiAuA89U8:TvE8LYPC7H8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=4ZEiAuA89U8:TvE8LYPC7H8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/4ZEiAuA89U8\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 07 Jun 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=4ZEiAuA89U8:TvE8LYPC7H8:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"49888f7436a59b8709676dadcdd65fd2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn83@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-37-237_0c284bc6d8fa6eb9.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=4ZEiAuA89U8:TvE8LYPC7H8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn83@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-37-237_0c284bc6d8fa6eb9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/4ZEiAuA89U8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn47@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-57-465_c55755a72041aa90.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476256},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Go Mummy - I'm trying to capture these as a I go along in my github repo - which makes me wonder how on earth developers in the 80s managed to code both on a single process system (i.e. no multi-tasking) and without any code control. Wow.</p>\n<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://my.matterport.com/show/?m=NeiMEZa9d93&#38;mls=1\">my.matterport.com</a></em></p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a 15:44:36 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=Iqu8XPK20RU:b4kpCrabrW0:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"17856537965be334a5a5456feade442b","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn68@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-37-402_27523d86ffb52e34.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=Iqu8XPK20RU:b4kpCrabrW0:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn68@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-37-402_27523d86ffb52e34.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/Iqu8XPK20RU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn2@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-57-299_309d9b9c4e004df0.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476261},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"How to pad a file with specific bytes [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/glEOnYrdaVo/how-to-pad-a-file-with-specific-bytes","description":"\n<p>On my ever onward quest for new useless knowledge I wanted to know how to change a file's length and pad it with a specific byte value, on the command line.</p>\n<p>Funnily enough, I know how to do this with JavaScript in the browser pretty easily (for me), but the challenge was using tools fit for the job (and I didn't really want to use a JS engine to do the job).</p>\n<h2>dd my old friend</h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://manpage.me/?q=dd\"><code>dd</code></a> is a command line tool that can generate files, useful in fact when you want to <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2007/10/29/delay-the-dom-ready-event-generate-a-dummy-file\">create dummy files</a> (as I was 13 years agoâ€¦ ðŸ˜±).</p>\n<p>To generate the dummy data, <code>dd</code> reads from <code>/dev/zero</code> (which gives you a stream of the null byte, <code>0x00</code>).</p>\n<p>Using <code>dd</code> I need to:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Copy the source file</li>\n<li>Add X new bytes to the end of the source file until it reaches Y length</li>\n<li>Ensure those new bytes are the one I defined, the null zero byte isn't good enough</li>\n</ul>\n<p>First task before I use <code>dd</code> is: create a stream of the byte I want, let's say <code>0xFC</code> (252 in decimal).</p>\n<h2>A stream of bytes</h2>\n<p>There's actually two tools I could use here. The first (and the one I'll use) is <a href=\"https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/dev/zero\"><code>/dev/zero</code></a> the alternative is to use <code>yes</code> with an argument (so <code>yes 1</code> will repeat <code>1\\n</code> over and over) - but with <code>yes</code> I'd need to strip the new line, then change the <code>1</code> character.</p>\n<p>So, pipe <code>/dev/zero</code> to <code>tr</code> and transform the zero byte into <code>0xFC</code>. Of course, <code>tr</code> doesn't do hex, it does octal (base 8), so I need:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">tr '\\0' '\\374' &#60; /dev/zero\n</code></pre>\n<p>Let's double check this is the right value, by looking at the first 16 bytes as hex:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">tr '\\0' '\\374' &#60; /dev/zero | head -c 16 | hexdump\n0000000 c3 bc c3 bc c3 bc c3 bc c3 bc c3 bc c3 bc c3 bc\n0000010\n</code></pre>\n<p>Urmâ€¦spot a problem? I've got <code>0xC3BC</code> as a repeating word which is <em>not</em> what I was after. From what I could gather, this is because <code>tr</code> is used to translate strings, and the default language it's using is UTF8 whichâ€¦ the byte 0xFC is outside of a normal range, or, something - I'm never quite going to understand UTF8 fully (<a href=\"https://http203.libsyn.com/how-to-avoid-getting-utfd-by-text-encodings\">but these two do</a>).</p>\n<p>The solution is to switch the language <code>tr</code> is using:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">LC_CTYPE=C tr '\\0' '\\374' &#60; /dev/zero | head -c 16 | hexdump\n0000000 fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc fc\n0000010\n</code></pre>\n<p>That's better. Now let's pipe that to <code>dd</code></p>\n<h2>Generating fixed length files</h2>\n<p>My aim is to take a file that has an arbitrary length with existing data, and pad it to 16K and any padded bytes must be <code>0xFC</code>.</p>\n<p>To create a 16K file (called <code>output.bin</code>) with <code>dd</code> using our byte, the line is:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">$ LC_CTYPE=C tr '\\0' '\\374' &#60; /dev/zero | dd of=output.bin bs=16k count=1\n</code></pre>\n<p>This means our <em>blocksize</em> <code>bs=</code> is 16k (<code>dd</code> supports shorthand for file sizes) and we want one block of 16k. Alternatively I could have <code>bs=1k count=16</code> to make 16 blocks of 1k - hopefully you get the idea.</p>\n<p>Except this makes a whole file, I need to <em>add</em> to a file. This is multipart task with a calculator handy.</p>\n<p>Instead of 16K of data, I need <code>16K - $currentFileLength</code>. To get this, I need two things: <code>expr</code> (for the maths) and <code>stat</code> (to get the file size accurately).</p>\n<p>To test this, I use the following command:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">$ expr 16384 - $(stat -f &#34;%Dz&#34; input.bin)\n15488\n</code></pre>\n<p>To generate a zero byte for 15,488 bytes I'll use <code>dd</code> to fill with a blocksize of 1 byte and for a count of 15,488 bytes:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">dd if=/dev/zero bs=1 count=$(expr 16384 - $(stat -f &#34;%Dz&#34; input.bin))\n</code></pre>\n<p>But this is still zero bytes, so streaming through <code>tr</code> converts to <code>0xFC</code>:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">dd if=/dev/zero bs=1 count=$(expr 16384 - $(stat -f &#34;%Dz&#34; input.bin)) \\\n | LC_CTYPE=C tr '\\0' '\\374'\n</code></pre>\n<p>Now I have 15,488 bytes of <code>0xFC</code>.</p>\n<p>So now I need to take the contents of <code>input.bin</code> and the generated output from <code>dd</code> and concatenate the two blocks of content into a final file called <code>output.bin</code>.</p>\n<p>That looks like this:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-sh\">cat input.bin \\\n &#60;( dd if=/dev/zero bs=1 count=$(\\\n      expr 16384 - $(stat -f &#34;%Dz&#34; input.bin)\n    ) | LC_CTYPE=C tr '\\0' '\\374'\n ) &#62; output.bin\n</code></pre>\n<p>A bit of a mouthful, but it puts together all the parts, then uses stream redirection to add <code>dd</code> to the output of <code>cat</code> and the concatenated result is put in <code>output.bin</code>, which is: exactly 16K large, contains 896 bytes of the original <code>input.bin</code> data and then follows <code>0xFC</code> for all the subsequent bytes.</p>\n<p>Ah yes, that old &#34;command line rabbit hole&#34;.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2020/06/17/how-to-pad-a-file-with-specific-bytes\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=glEOnYrdaVo:Jt5_wmS0Utc:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=glEOnYrdaVo:Jt5_wmS0Utc:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/glEOnYrdaVo\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 17 Jun 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=glEOnYrdaVo:Jt5_wmS0Utc:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"863efc871cef98096fd06f9a6d216935","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn71@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-381_88efdb57203aec51.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=glEOnYrdaVo:Jt5_wmS0Utc:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn71@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-381_88efdb57203aec51.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/glEOnYrdaVo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn64@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-57-293_bd4974c1a30eaaa1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476254},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 I've been tinkering with an Oh Mummy clone for my Spectrum in NextBASIC, and although it's been more than a month I've been tinkering, I've decided to start a dev log for my own thoughts and diary-like note taking.</p>\n<h2>Links and newsletters</h2>\n<p>Along with TIL and devlog, my links that I annotate are also included in the feed. These are links that I generally put more effort into bookmarking and indicating what I think is useful about them (to me or you), so this won't just be me hitting &#34;like&#34; on twitter all over the place.</p>\n<p>I also ran a newsletter for a little over 2 years. For some reason or another I decided to take a break at the start of this year (probably laziness) but they're also included in the feed and are more <em>digest'y</em> than full blog posts.</p>\n<h2>At home here too</h2>\n<p>All of this new (sort of) content has a home on this blog:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://remysharp.com/archive\">The whole shebang</a> - <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/feed.xml\">dedicated RSS</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://remysharp.com/\">blog</a> - <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/blog.xml\">dedicated RSS (of <em>just</em> blog posts)</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til\">til</a> - <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til.xml\">dedicated RSS</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog\">devlog</a> - <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog.xml\">dedicated RSS</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://remysharp.com/links\">links</a> - <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/links.xml\">dedicated RSS</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://remysharp.com/newsletters/#content\">newsletters</a> - <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/newsletters/\">email subscription</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p>The whole feed also has an indicator tag to show whether the type of post it is (so if you're an RSS subscriber you can skim over things like the devlog if it doesn't interest you).</p>\n<p>These entires also appear in search results on my site and on the archive pages (which now look like I've been super busy writing, which makes me feel good but isn't quite representative of the truth!).</p>\n<hr>\n<p>I kind of feel like I've ruffled all the pillows in my website and sunk my butt right down to make a cozy <em>remy shaped</em> dent here. end I inlined every call, which is horrid to look at, but the performance went right back up again. The lesson: no functions.</p>\n<p>â€¦which makes me thing I need some kind of compiler to inline everything, but that might be for another day.</p>\n<p>I also got the tomb open visuals working, and next need to add the graphics for the scroll, pharaoh, key and treasure:</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-06-01.png\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p>One growing concern is that the game is playable with 3 baddies, but at 9 (which isn't a stretch to have going on in the original game), it gets very clunky, and I'm wondering if I can optimise the code further by throwing away the mummy array (that holds each mummy data) and move to first class variables for each iteration, ie. <code>%x</code> becomes the mummy's x position - and I back the data into memory using <code>PEEK</code> and <code>POKE</code>.</p>\n<p>It would reduce the number of array lookups and would reduce/remove a lot of maths that goes on during the mummy logic.</p>\n<p>It's just a rather large changeâ€¦and a headache.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/go-mummy/2020-06-01\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=mtAeBg9T9fY:QBDqa2fsmDU:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=mtAeBg9T9fY:QBDqa2fsmDU:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/mtAeBg9T9fY\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 01 Jun 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-06-01.png","linkMd5":"0e87167058b997e48234bde0ebf3e67b","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-36-901_765933c05589511b.webp","destWidth":1200,"destHeight":933,"sourceBytes":50542,"destBytes":60774,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-06-01.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-36-901_765933c05589511b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=mtAeBg9T9fY:QBDqa2fsmDU:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn40@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-57-386_ddb912f5331cfdee.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/mtAeBg9T9fY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn7@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-58-135_6777d739ec002758.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476259},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Go Mummy - I <em>could</em> check the whole of this array each time the tomb is surrounded, but it makes more sense to add which are the &#34;winning&#34; tombs to the tomb array(20) I already have.</p>\n<p>The tomb array itself holds it's state in bit values. As such, the current line of code for marking one side of a tomb as &#34;completed&#34; looks like this (horribly):</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token keyword\">IF</span> <span class=\"token operator\">%</span>k <span class=\"token keyword\">THEN</span> <span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>g<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>g<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span>&#38;@<span class=\"token number\">11111101</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>h<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>h<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span>&#38;@<span class=\"token number\">11110111</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> <span class=\"token comment\">; new line for readability</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">ELSE</span> <span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>g<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>g<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span>&#38;@<span class=\"token number\">11111011</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>h<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span>T<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span>h<span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span>&#38;@<span class=\"token number\">11111110</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>The low <a href=\"https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nibble\">nibble</a> represent the side of the tomb that has been completed, and the high nibble for whether the tomb has been unlocked already:</p>\n<pre><code>0x01=top\n0x02=right\n0x04=bottom\n0x08=left\n0xF0=tomb has been unlocked\n</code></pre>\n<p>So the <code>IF</code> statement from earlier is always run and always applies the logical <code>&#38;</code> but this is to create consistent timings. Normally, in modern coding, I'd avoid unnecessary code execution, but with NextBASIC to get the game to run at a consistent speed, I'm making sure that each loop does roughly the same amount of work.</p>\n<p>Thus far I'm only using 8 bits of the value to indicate the status of the tomb and I need to be able to flag the tomb to say what's contained inside of it, either a scroll, a mummy, a key, a tomb or nothing at all. I could keep all this data inside a single byte, but the integers in NextBASIC as 16bit so I could also expand out to the high byte to store the value of the tomb.</p>\n<p>Meh. I prefer to be efficient, so how about this:</p>\n<pre><code>0x00-0x04=tomb contents\n0x08=tomb has been unlocked\n0x10=top\n0x20=right\n0x40=bottom\n0x80=left\n</code></pre>\n<p>This shifts around where the data is stored, but I put the wall status on the high nibble for simplicity, so that I can then do something like <code>%T = %T + INT (key)</code> and set <code>key = 3</code> somewhere as a constant (though in reality I'll stick to integer expressions).</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/go-mummy/2020-05-24\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=rUEg6gUsvUU:cykIa16Mdz4:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=rUEg6gUsvUU:cykIa16Mdz4:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/rUEg6gUsvUU\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 24 May 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=rUEg6gUsvUU:cykIa16Mdz4:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"181d3ddd96f356de8657e05c3690cbaa","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn37@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-397_bd1a661f5581d46b.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=rUEg6gUsvUU:cykIa16Mdz4:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn37@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-397_bd1a661f5581d46b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/rUEg6gUsvUU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn35@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-58-137_5f2b5c7eed9e5a6e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476261},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Go Mummy - 7-Jul 2020 [devlog/go-mummy]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/NpXxCAExnJc/2020-07-07","description":"<p>This most recent round of development has been dedicated to squashing out bugs and investing in performance optimisations.</p>\n<p>What's particularly fun about NextBASIC is that it's so close to the metal (as it were) - NextBASIC -&#62; interpreter -&#62; machine code - that it has a heavy hand in the code design that I work with.</p>\n<p>I'm used to JavaScript which goes through part compile, part interpreted along with a lot of JIT'ting and hot path optimisation. No such pleasantries with NextBASIC.</p>\n<p>A simple example is that in modern high level languages, I'd reduce my code reuse and refactor based on the rule that if a value or expression is used more than once, then it belongs in it's own variable or routine.</p>\n<p>Using that approach with NextBASIC comes at a cost, a cost that is immediately visible in the execution. Multiple routine calls slows down the runtime speed. Inlining code will always speed execution up (and this is also true of languages like JS).</p>\n<p>There's also the aspect of finding the absolute perfect fit of code for the problem - which again in JavaScript (or other languages) the perfect fit isn't always necessary (and sometimes discouraged and it makes it harder to read later). But this approach makes me think carefully about how the system works at it's lowest level.</p>\n<p>A recent change is that I removed all the <code>CLS</code> calls from my game. This clears the screen. But the ROM routine <a href=\"https://speccy.xyz/rom/asm/0d6b\">does a lot more</a> than &#34;just clearing the screen&#34;.</p>\n<p>Instead, now I'm writing bytes directly to the screen memory which has a near instant effect and there's no longer a wipe-and-wait delay:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token comment\">; bank 9-11 is the thirds of the screen memory in layer 2</span>\n<span class=\"token comment\">; bank 25 contains 1/3 of a screen header</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">25</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">COPY</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">TO</span> <span class=\"token number\">9</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token comment\">; \"Oh Mummy header\"</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">10</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">ERASE</span> <span class=\"token number\">252</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token comment\">; Set the middle third to yellow</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">11</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">ERASE</span> <span class=\"token operator\">%</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span><span class=\"token variable\">$3000</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span><span class=\"token number\">252</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token comment\">; REM 0-0x3000 as yellow</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">BANK</span> <span class=\"token number\">11</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">ERASE</span> <span class=\"token operator\">%</span><span class=\"token variable\">$3000</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span><span class=\"token operator\">%</span><span class=\"token variable\">$1000</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> <span class=\"token comment\">; last 4k is black</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>The bugs I've been squashing have been mostly been subtle issues that (hopefully) make the difference between &#34;okay cool&#34; and &#34;oh, that's odd&#34;.</p>\n<p>Here's a fun bit of debugging to make sure the footsteps are positioned correctly:</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-07.gif\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<p>The most recent fix I was most proud of is a control hack. If the player tries to move right, but there's a wall in the way, it'll continue moving in the direction they were previously facing until they're free to move right. This hack means skimming around corners is much more natural - an invisible change to the player, but it felt <em>sticky</em> (or broken) when the player would be stuck hitting wall before a corner.</p>\n<p>The outstanding tasks before the game is in a (first draft) complete state are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>(required) Game over - Win state</li>\n<li>(required) Hi-score table</li>\n<li>(feat) Change colours of tombs between each level</li>\n<li>(feat) &#34;Get outta there&#34; / &#34;now find the archaeologist&#34; / &#34;find that key!&#34; marquee</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Which doesn't feel too far away!</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/go-mummy/2020-07-07\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=NpXxCAExnJc:EaB2SicTyM8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=NpXxCAExnJc:EaB2SicTyM8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/NpXxCAExnJc\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 07 Jul 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-07.gif","linkMd5":"bf7d7c482cffcd8bf4a78c4b8987f9e1","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn4@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-56-297_3fbb626553b60a08.webp","destWidth":1280,"destHeight":720,"sourceBytes":124503,"destBytes":62710,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://remysharp.com/images/devlog/ohm-2020-07-07.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn4@2020_1/2020/08/24/21-44-56-297_3fbb626553b60a08.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=NpXxCAExnJc:EaB2SicTyM8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn9@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-57-562_548dba91ae82154d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/NpXxCAExnJc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn28@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-57-296_f5ab659194d77e69.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476251},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"The Bell Jar [book]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/az62Q5YRXys/the-bell-jar","description":"<p>This is a hard book to read, partly for the confused start, but also the very real ending. A deep insight into clinical depression.</p>\n<p>I have to admit that in reading this book I really struggled to enjoy it - and not because it of the nature of the book, but because it felt like I was bouncing around inside of Sylvia Plath's head in a random jumbled up, non linear fashion.</p>\n<p>In fact, I'd say the first third of the book is almost entirely that. The mini stories that occur don't really finish, and as we were journeying through one recounted story, I'd find we'd quickly make a sharp turn and begin a new journey.</p>\n<p>The middle third starts to become a bit more pieced together but the book was struggling to win me over. Esther Greenwood (which I'd read earlier The Bell Jar was semi-autobiographical) wanted to kill herself. The way that this third goes on read almost childish and, for my shame, I was beginning to hope the character &#34;just get on with it&#34;.</p>\n<p>It was also that the first section of the book painted an extremely successful character and the character in the second part was very much the opposite end of the spectrum and the different was jarring and hard to consolidate (as a reader).</p>\n<p>Suffice to say, she does indeed attempt suicide. For the final third of the book she is institutionalised and undergoes therapy but also electroconvulsive therapy (ECT). The ECT isn't glorified nor is it vilified which was interesting and challenging (particularly with the story being semi-autobiographical).</p>\n<p>The last third takes its time and walks gently through the journey that she takes during her institutionalised. None of this part of the book is glamourised and she doesn't make some magical recovery.</p>\n<p>It's slow, gentle and unsure. Even as Esther finally reaches her board review to see if she can leave the institution, she herself is unconvinced that anything has changed, but something is certainly at rest in her.</p>\n<p>The last part of the book definitely calls for reflection and helped to give me an insight into those who struggle with existing. There's rarely some grand purpose that drives them to death by suicide, and indeed in Esther's case there's nothing that particularly explain <em>why</em> she wanted to end her life.</p>\n<p>There's a moment with her medical supervisor where Esther says that she hates her mother. This is after their last encounter - and her mother isn't bad in the slightest, it's that her mother wants to know what she had done wrong to have not been able to help protect her daughter from these feelings. The supervisor (slash therapist) says, &#34;I believe you do&#34;. She doesn't try to sympathies or give Esther another point of view. This line surprised me, in a believable way.</p>\n<p>And as the book ends, Esther is reunited with her mother, and her mother, naively says she just wants to forget about it all and move forward from this, healthier time. To which Esther writes that her mother may want to forget and that perhaps Esther might forget those feelings:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>Maybe forgetfulness, like a kind snow, should numb and cover them. But they were part of me. They were my landscape.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Having dealings with depression myself, and shock grief of the worst kind, it really doesn't go away, and it isn't forgotten. It's as Plath writes: it becomes part of your landscape.</p>\n<hr>\n<p>This is a hard book to read, partly for the confused start, but also the very real ending. Made harder by knowing that Sylvia Plath died by suicide the same year of this book's release.</p>\n<p>Plath described the book (to her mother) as:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>a pot boiler really, but I think it will show how isolated a person feels when he is suffering a breakdown.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Indeed that's the experience of the last third of the book.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/books/2020/the-bell-jar\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=az62Q5YRXys:CiT56c4GdFM:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=az62Q5YRXys:CiT56c4GdFM:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/az62Q5YRXys\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 26 Jul 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=az62Q5YRXys:CiT56c4GdFM:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"8ec1f54f55dcd8eb5579d49d3b58f623","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn91@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-378_980fd3b2225cca4e.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=az62Q5YRXys:CiT56c4GdFM:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn91@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-36-378_980fd3b2225cca4e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/az62Q5YRXys":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn75@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-57-398_cb5059759fc9f9dd.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476248},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"\"Share the knowledge for free\" [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/qJCzbmOIPso/share-the-knowledge-for-free","description":"\n<p>That title is in &#34;air quotes&#34; - just to be clear. I'm writing this so I don't have to repeat myself, because this sentiment has come up over and over and over. Not just for me, but for you, for your peers, your friends and many other anonymous creators out there.</p>\n<p>&#34;Share the knowledge for free&#34; - anon.</p>\n<p>The short reply is: no.</p>\n<p>But, sure, let's take a moment to discuss this.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.giphy.com/media/3o6ZtokgzQv6ThHzj2/giphy.gif\" alt=\"\"></p>\n<h2>No?</h2>\n<p>Just to clear up the obvious first: we have bills to pay. I have a mortgage. I need food. I have kids and dependents.</p>\n<p>I am able to work, therefore I do, and that work brings in money to our family and with that money we support our lives. Thank god my partner and I are able to work. I know there's others who are less fortunate and struggle at this basic need.</p>\n<p>This isn't money grabbing nor taking advantage of entity handing over the money. Money, in this particular reality, is core to survival. You know this, we all know this.</p>\n<h2>I didn't say &#34;work for free&#34;</h2>\n<p>That's right, you said give away your knowledge for free. Sure, speaking is &#34;free&#34; (mostly). But acquiring that knowledge was not a free process for me.</p>\n<p>It either took hours and hours and hours and actually <em>years</em> of learning. Along the way that involved buying books, buying software, coding and creating - all activities that no one is paying me for.</p>\n<p>Yet still that knowledge is now in me, surely I can give that away? Well, if I can stick a Matrix-like spike in the back of my head and connect it to yours, then sure, I'd be willing to do that.</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://remysharp.com/images/i-no-kung-fu.jpg\" alt=\"Neo from the Matrix learning kung fu from a brain download\"></p>\n<p>Except in reality we need to create a medium to transfer knowledge. This has costs, here's some of those costs off the top of my head for content I create:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>The time spent writing content (long)</li>\n<li>Time spent creating videos or audio (again, long)</li>\n<li>Creating supporting websites for said content</li>\n<li>Hosting fees for content (particularly video is yearly)</li>\n</ul>\n<p>All this time is time spent not earning a living too.</p>\n<p>So, I'm saying, for the record, &#34;sharing your knowledge for free&#34; is a misnomer. There is no &#34;free&#34; for me, nor for you.</p>\n<p>This post is pretty much redundant, but maybe I'll be able to save myself the time (and thus cost) of replying this same sentiment every time I'm faced with this.</p>\n<h2>Free is not the default</h2>\n<p>There's many many examples of people sharing their work for free. I applaud you. I'm in this group, jsbin, nodemon, this blog and many other projects - but this is not a hard requirement of being part of the web or the world.</p>\n<p>Free is not the default, it never was. I value your work. I believe we should be paid, and I've written about this before in <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2014/03/07/youre-paying-to-speak\">You're Paying to Speak</a> and <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2019/07/30/buy-the-coffee\">Buy the coffee</a>. I <em>love</em> paying for people's work on <a href=\"https://itch.io\">itch.io</a> (I've bought an ungodly number of asset libraries for ideas that I'll probably never get around to).</p>\n<p>I <em>love</em> supporting other people's work when I can. I'll continue to do so whilst I can afford to.</p>\n<p>So get paid. Ask to be paid.</p>\n<p><strong>Your work is valuable and your time and experience is even more so.</strong></p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2020/07/03/share-the-knowledge-for-free\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=qJCzbmOIPso:GlQrzUoIyqk:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=qJCzbmOIPso:GlQrzUoIyqk:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"
