00:00:00 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"https://media.giphy.com/media/3o6ZtokgzQv6ThHzj2/giphy.gif","linkMd5":"6d4a945a4c74978587f3f30c5d581152","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn96@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-37-308_4a90e610ac1028dc.webp","destWidth":480,"destHeight":262,"sourceBytes":1295249,"destBytes":194226,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://media.giphy.com/media/3o6ZtokgzQv6ThHzj2/giphy.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn96@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-37-308_4a90e610ac1028dc.webp","https://remysharp.com/images/i-no-kung-fu.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn32@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-57-873_33a37dfd355f718d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=qJCzbmOIPso:GlQrzUoIyqk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn22@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-57-309_33842326726e8e73.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/qJCzbmOIPso":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn84@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-58-199_1bdf9b98d0fa6ed7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476263},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"A px is not a px [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/72IuAZ7A0Kw/a-px-is-not-a-px","description":"\n<p>Recently I was trying to extract some glyphs from some various fonts and in doing so I had a fundamental assumption challenged and dispelled.</p>\n<p>A <code>px</code> in terms of fonts, is not a pixel. Or certainly not in the way I was using them.</p>\n<p>For as long as I can remember I've used <code>px</code> for my CSS fonts. I tried with <code>em</code>s and usually ran into some sizing issues (better devs than me know how to use them properly). I had a lot of success with <code>rem</code>s (not only because clearly they're named after yours trulyâ€¦not), but if you asked me yesterday how to a make a font sized at 16 pixels, I'd have said 'font-size: 16px`.</p>\n<p>If I'm honest, it's close enough and when a font size isn't <em>quite</em> right, I adjust. I tweak the font size, I tweak the line height, I tweak margins and padding until it looks right.</p>\n<p>From a fully technical and exact perspective though, I didn't know what I was talking about!</p>\n<h2>When I realised</h2>\n<p>I was trying to render tiny fonts, no larger than 8 pixels wide into a canvas, and extract the pixel data (for a ZX Spectrum project). So I unwittingly set the font size in the 2D drawing API to <code>8px</code> and ran the <code>fillText</code> method only to be faced with text that either didn't fit in the 8x8 square or was way too small.</p>\n<p>I <em>thought</em> (incorrectly) that <code>8px</code> meant the font would be 8 pixels tall. So utterly wrong.</p>\n<p>This is also compounded by the fact that when you draw on a canvas, you need to specify the X and Y coordinate of the baseline - the specification suggests X/Y is the top left corner, but this isn't the case as drawing text in a canvas draws <em>upwards</em> so with <code>x:0, y:0</code> you get nearly completely clipped text.</p>\n<p>So I would have hoped the way to get the text to render on the canvas would be to add the pixel height of the font: <code>x:0, y:8</code> but as we already know, the height of the font isn't 8 pixels.</p>\n<h2>What makes the height of a font?</h2>\n<p>I won't pretend to fully understand it (yet) but there's an <a href=\"https://iamvdo.me/en/blog/css-font-metrics-line-height-and-vertical-align\">excellent breakdown post by Vincent De Oliveira</a> that examines how to align 100px to a font height and how it breaks up. The practical example that De Oliverira gets into is if they want to place a checkbox image aligned with the text. It's not as easy as it might first sound.</p>\n<p>Also, more practically, there is the <a href=\"https://seek-oss.github.io/capsize/\">Capsize</a> project that allows you to upload a font or select an existing Google font, and the page will read in the metadata about the font and help you adjust values to get the height of the font to best suit your needs.</p>\n<p><strong>As it turns out, in a lot of cases, when I'm thinking of the <em>height</em> of a font, I'm actually thinking about the height of a capital letter, which is the ascender in font metrics.</strong></p>\n<h2>Bits of a font</h2>\n<p>In my side projects I spend a lot of time looking at binary data and parsing it in JavaScript so it made sense that I should poke around in the font to see if I could find these values myself.</p>\n<p>Thus far I've only looked at TrueType fonts. The font file is structured as so:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Header (12 bytes) - which includes the font file signature and directly after includes the 32bit table count</li>\n<li>Array of tables - each table includes: tag name (4 characters padded), checksum, file offset and length</li>\n</ol>\n<p>With these small bits of information we will have an array of all the font tables that are included in the file. The tables of interests are required in the file format (according to <a href=\"https://developer.apple.com/fonts//TrueType-Reference-Manual/RM06/Chap6.html#Overview\">Apple's documentation</a>) and I want to look inside the tables: <code>OS/2</code>, <code>hhea</code> and <code>head</code>.</p>\n<p>These tables can appear in any order in the file and have variable length - both depending on the tag name but also the version of the table.</p>\n<p>To extract the information out of the file, first the file is uploaded into the browser and using the <code>FileReader</code> API I'll get an <code>ArrayBuffer</code> of the bytes:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\">input<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function-variable function\">onchange</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token parameter\">event</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=></span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> file <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> event<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>target<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>files<span class=\"token punctuation\">[</span><span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">]</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> reader <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">FileReader</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  reader<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function-variable function\">onload</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token parameter\">event</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=></span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n    <span class=\"token comment\">// do something with the buffer</span>\n    <span class=\"token function\">handleData</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>event<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>target<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>result<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  reader<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">readAsArrayBuffer</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>file<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>For instance, to extract the capital height, I can create a view on the buffer and extract the 16bit value I need:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-js\"><span class=\"token keyword\">function</span> <span class=\"token function\">handleData</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token parameter\">buffer</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> view <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">DataView</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>buffer<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> tableCount <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> view<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">getUint16</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token number\">5</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token boolean\">true</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">let</span> capitalHeight <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">null</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n\n  <span class=\"token comment\">// use a decoder to read the tag 4 character field</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> decoder <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">new</span> <span class=\"token class-name\">TextDecoder</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">let</span> ptr <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token number\">12</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> <span class=\"token comment\">// where the header ends</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">for</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token keyword\">let</span> i <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token number\">0</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> i <span class=\"token operator\">&#60;</span> tableCount<span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> i<span class=\"token operator\">++</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n    <span class=\"token comment\">// the tag is 4 characters long</span>\n    <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> tag <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> decoder<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">decode</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>data<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">slice</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>ptr<span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> ptr <span class=\"token operator\">+</span> <span class=\"token number\">4</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n\n    <span class=\"token comment\">// `offset` is where we find the table data in the file</span>\n    <span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> offset <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> view<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">getUint32</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>ptr <span class=\"token operator\">+</span> <span class=\"token number\">8</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n\n    <span class=\"token keyword\">if</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>tag <span class=\"token operator\">===</span> <span class=\"token string\">'OS/2'</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n      <span class=\"token comment\">// cap height sits 88 bytes from the start of the header</span>\n      capitalHeight <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> view<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">getInt16</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>offset <span class=\"token operator\">+</span> <span class=\"token number\">88</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token operator\">/</span> <span class=\"token number\">1000</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n    <span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\n\n    <span class=\"token comment\">// table headers are 16 bytes long</span>\n    ptr <span class=\"token operator\">+=</span> <span class=\"token number\">16</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Now I can use the <code>capitalHeight</code> as I feel fit and all in the browser if I wanted to do work dynamically.</p>\n<p>In practice, if the aim is to align text, then it makes sense to collect the font metric data ahead of time with a tool like <a href=\"https://seek-oss.github.io/capsize/\">Capsize</a> or if that resource ever disappears I've extended the code I wrote earlier to a barebones <a href=\"https://font-size.isthe.link/\">TTF metrics extraction</a> tool.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a The process being copy the png image to an HTML5 canvas element, then extract the pixels then generate the bitmap header and arrange the image data appropriately.</p>\n<p>I've always known about indexed palettes and their existence (as an option during exporting in Photoshop) but never really knew how they worked.</p>\n<p>After rolling it by hand (without compression), it's rather obvious - though only in retrospect!</p>\n<p>Generally (apparently) 8bit and below Bitmaps will include their own palette. This (I think/imagine) is because the size of the palette (in bytes) at 16bits would be larger than the data representing the pixels, so in 16bit and above, the actual colour is in the pixel byte (I could be totally wrong, but that'll be a TIL on 16bit images!).</p>\n<p>An 8bit image (or smaller, such as 4bit) is structured thusly:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Header - contains dimensions, colour information, offsets, etc. 56 bytes.</li>\n<li>Palette - if the colour count isn't defined (i.e. 0 in the header), then this will be 4 * 256 (4 being alpha, blue, green, red - yes, in that order).</li>\n<li>The pixel bytes referencing the palette</li>\n</ol>\n<p>So what's interesting is that the pixel bytes are single bytes from the range of 0-255 which is an index of the palette. The palette range can be anything with an RGBA range.</p>\n<p>A 4bit bitmap would use a &#34;nibble&#34; for the palette (and I'd expect it to be 512bytes, though I've not investigated them fully).</p>\n<p>So that's what indexed palette is. It's 1K of colour data and the actual pixel data <em>points</em> to the palette. Clever. Simple.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til/computing/index-bitmaps\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=tH6fB9TkTko:tGLAQz-F7Ik:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=tH6fB9TkTko:tGLAQz-F7Ik:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/tH6fB9TkTko\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 13 Jul 2020 13:19:29 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=tH6fB9TkTko:tGLAQz-F7Ik:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"5b44167204a19685c3d36a2f51414f53","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn79@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-37-227_b2bf1b8839530e83.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=tH6fB9TkTko:tGLAQz-F7Ik:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn79@2020_5/2020/08/24/21-44-37-227_b2bf1b8839530e83.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/tH6fB9TkTko":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn67@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-58-099_9bf2fab72bec8689.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476250},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"48K [til/spectrum]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/0v0svzjl5Ak/48k","description":"\n<p>I might have been slow on the uptake with this one, but I always wondered why the Spectrum 48K was 48K. Most computer's memory goes up in powers of 2, 16mb, 32mb, 64mb, etc. Sure, you can sometimes have a 16mb RAM chip along side 32mb but that isn't super common.</p>\n<p>Anyway, in reading Spectrum Machine Language for the Absolute Beginner (because ... I don't really know), I came across this:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>The maximum memory that can be accessed [in ZX Spectrum] by this instruction is only 64K! This means that all the memory - ROM, program, display, and free memory have to fit within 64K. On a &#34;16K Spectrum&#34; there is actually 16K used by the ROM and 16K of RAM making a total of 32K.</p>\n<p>The &#34;16K&#34; refers to the RAM part only. On the &#34;48K Spectrum&#34;, the same 16K of POM is present plus 48K of RAM making a total of 64K.</p>\n<p>It is not possible therefore for the Z80 to access more memory than is available on a 48K spectrum.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The ZX Spectrum used a single 16K ROM IC chip (the bit that held the operating system burnt into the chip), and then a bank of 16K via 8 2K ICs and another bank of 32K via 8 4K ICs.</p>\n<p>So that's a total of 64K, 65536 bytes of &#34;memory&#34;. 16K of which is ROM and the rest, 48K, is RAM. Hence the name, that stuck with me for 30 or so years.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til/spectrum/48k\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=0v0svzjl5Ak:M204YIvzwK8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=0v0svzjl5Ak:M204YIvzwK8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/0v0svzjl5Ak\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 09 Jun 2020 14:55:58 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=0v0svzjl5Ak:M204YIvzwK8:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"8178f025a953056d55b3f887d9e9c42e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn75@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-36-454_ec1e0e9b99d3a1c5.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=0v0svzjl5Ak:M204YIvzwK8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn75@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-36-454_ec1e0e9b99d3a1c5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/0v0svzjl5Ak":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn99@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-58-101_eeeb45bec43c1997.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476255},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Go Mummy - 28-Jul 2020 [devlog/go-mummy]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/0pKw0vB68S8/2020-07-28","description":"<p>After <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/oh-mummy/2020-07-20\">last week's failure</a> in sound this week(end) was a total win over sound ðŸ’ª</p>\n<p>I knew the game played better with some audible feedback and I also knew that the only way I could pull it off in NextBASIC was to use the interrupt handler at the machine code level. I'd previously tried and failed with <a href=\"https://speccy.xyz/opcodes/im/\"><code>im 2</code></a> but this time I looked at the native <code>DRIVER</code> support that NextOS offers a hook in to the <code>im 1</code> interrupt.</p>\n<p>The short version is, once I groked the <a href=\"https://gitlab.com/thesmog358/tbblue/-/blob/master/src/asm/border/border.asm\">border example</a> I managed to port the <a href=\"https://shiru.untergrund.net/software.shtml#old\">AYFX player</a> from Shiru to a driver.</p>\n<p>The bulk of my code involved handling the driver calls and make sure to swap in the user bank during the routines and swap back to the original bank into the slot I was using.</p>\n<p>I made some silly mistakes in the code, but managed to debug successfully using <a href=\"http://cspect.org/\">Cspect</a>, things like <code>ld a, (addr)</code> must be read (and thought of) as &#34;load a <em>with</em> addr&#34; (and not &#34;load a <em>into</em> addr&#34;!).</p>\n<p>My bank swapping code looks like this:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-asm\">MMU6_C000_NR_56\t\tequ $56\n\n; ************************************************\n; backup_bank\n; Take the current bank in MMU 6 and store the value\n; in (active_bank) for later restore.\n; ************************************************\nbackup_bank:\n  push      af        ; make a backup of A\n  ld        bc, $243b ; select NEXT register\n  in        a,(c)     ; save register state\n  ld        (saved_reg), a\n  ld        a, MMU6_C000_NR_56\n  out       (c),a\n  inc       b             ; $253b to access (read or write) value\n  in        a,(c)\n  ld        (active_bank),a\n  dec       b         ; $243B\n  ld        a,2\nsaved_reg equ $-1     ; this points saved_reg to the `2` above\n  out       (c),a     ; just in case IRQ was in between registry work\n  pop       af\n  ret\n\n; ************************************************\n; activate_user_bank\n; Switches in a user defined bank into MMU6\n; ************************************************\nactivate_user_bank:\n  call      backup_bank\n  ld        a, (ayfx_bank)\n  nextreg   MMU6_C000_NR_56, a\n  ret\n\n; ************************************************\n; restore_bank\n; Returns the bank slot to it's original setting\n; ************************************************\nrestore_bank:\n  ld        a, (active_bank)\n  nextreg   MMU6_C000_NR_56, a\n  ret\n</code></pre>\n<p>The result: uninterrupted game play with sound effects ðŸŽ‰</p>\n<iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/i8GaIduecNk\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n<p>Now the bug list is looking pretty small, the priority is a graphics glitch on level 4 (which can also be seen at the end of the game over on the letter &#34;E&#34;), then the scoring system (with high scores) and thenâ€¦ and then we're there.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/devlog/go-mummy/2020-07-28\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Custom fonts across layers [til/spectrum]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/fh7j2nKn5V0/custom-fonts-across-layers","description":"\n<p>Custom fonts on the Spectrum require loading a font file (768 bytes of 8x8 bit data - 96 characters from 0x20 to 0x80) but it's reasonably straight forward:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token keyword\">LOAD</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"font.bin\"</span> CODE <span class=\"token number\">64000</span>\n<span class=\"token keyword\">POKE</span> <span class=\"token number\">23607</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span><span class=\"token number\">249</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>But this works on the &#34;regular&#34; ULA layer - to make this work on layer 1 or layer 2, you need some magic:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token keyword\">PRINT</span> CHR$ <span class=\"token number\">2</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Explained <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/groups/ZXNextBasic/?post_id=834716357054705\">here</a> by Gary Lancaster, author of NextBASIC:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>You can replace the standard font for LAYER 0 by loading a standard 768-byte character set into memory and using:\nDPOKE 23606,address-256</p>\n<p>This can then be used to replace the standard 8-bit font for all other layers with:</p>\n<p>PRINT CHR$ 2</p>\n<p>And, if desired, you can generate the other sizes (3- to 7-bit) from this with:</p>\n<p>PRINT CHR$ 3</p>\n<p>(You must be in LAYER 1 or LAYER 2 for these two commands to take effect).</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The 256 offset is because the first character in the font is a space, set at ascii 32, and the glyphs are 8 bytes, so 32*8 = 256 offset.</p>\n<p>There's a better explanation of the <a href=\"https://spectrumcomputing.co.uk/forums/viewtopic.php?p=29248#p29248\">256 offset here</a> and setting the 16bit address.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a 20:48:31 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=W1JM2YR63g4:fQTrUHnlmdk:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"7e8e84249493a727d79584d33aa2cc1e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn41@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-36-404_1ff8f55eea581d03.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=W1JM2YR63g4:fQTrUHnlmdk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn41@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-36-404_1ff8f55eea581d03.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/W1JM2YR63g4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn52@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-58-180_d4b4d704271b4ae8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476260},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Works offline [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/8ITTjXZrRbg/works-offline","description":"\n<p>So many web sites work offline and we don't know it. It's kind of a beautiful aspect of the P in PWA: the web sites are progressively enhanced to be available even without an internet connection.</p>\n<p>Yet browsers won't tell us so. More on that in a bit. How do we tell our visitors our sites work offline. How do we tell our visitors that they don't need an app because it's no more capable than the URL they're on right now?</p>\n<p>I've created a Github issue (by way of creating an open forum) with a call for ideas and collaboration.</p>\n<p>Please, if you're a designer, iconographer, tinkerer, please contribute your ideas: <strong><a href=\"https://github.com/works-offline/logo/issues/1\">github#works-offline/logo/issues/1</a></strong></p>\n<p>I created the issue and the repo, but this isn't mine. In fact I immediately made <a href=\"https://github.com/works-offline/logo/issues/2\">issue 2</a> to that effect. This is an effort that requires us, the makers of the web, to take matters into our own hands.</p>\n<p>Creating a visual cue to offline capability isn't a new thing and I'm certainly not the first. The most recent large waves came in the form of the <a href=\"http://offlinefirst.org/\">Offline First initiative</a> which is already over 5 years old and <a href=\"http://hood.ie/blog/say-hello-to-offline-first.html\">introduced by Hoodie</a>. I remember <a href=\"https://alistapart.com/article/offline-first/\">A List Apart bringing support</a> (albeit via an article) which created some great momentum.</p>\n<p>Yet we're 5 years on and our visitors still don't realise how capable our sites are. Hell, I'd call myself pretty savvy but I didn't think for a moment that <a href=\"https://lodash.com/docs/4.17.15\">lodash's documentation</a> would work offline until I happened upon it by accident.</p>\n<p>I want to see some way that we can show, proudly, on our own web sites that our URLs work offline. As <a href=\"https://adactio.com/links/17137\">Jeremy reminds us</a>:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>â€¦seeing as browsers have completely dropped the ball on any kind of ambient badging, itâ€™s fair enough that we take matters into our own hands.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<h2>Branding matters</h2>\n<p>HTML. Web 2.0. Ajax. RSS. HTML5. PWA.</p>\n<p>These are â€¦ &#34;words&#34; that meaning to a select few individuals, and yet are recognised by a broad range of every day people.</p>\n<p>Some of these have <a href=\"https://www.w3.org/html/logo/faq.html\">logos</a> <a href=\"https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_web_application\">attached</a> to their ideas.</p>\n<p>But these are all examples of technical terms making it out into the wider world and becoming brand ambassadors for technical progress and innovation.</p>\n<p>Branding is incredibly powerful, as anyone hired to build an &#34;HTML5 web app&#34; knowing full well there may not actually be any &#34;HTML5&#34; in the resulting software. The exact definition doesn't matter. What matters is the hook.</p>\n<p>Often we just need a word to lean on to help people grasp the idea and run.</p>\n<p>What's also interesting is that a lot of these terms have a commonality that they don't mean just one thing. Just as &#34;XMLHttpRequest is only part of the Ajax equation&#34; as <a href=\"https://web.archive.org/web/20180822143943/https://www.adaptivepath.com/ideas/ajax-new-approach-web-applications/\">explained by Jessie James Garret</a> and as PWA doesn't <a href=\"https://infrequently.org/2015/06/progressive-apps-escaping-tabs-without-losing-our-soul/\">just mean &#34;service worker&#34;</a> (though technically without service workers there is no PWA).</p>\n<p>Likewise, &#34;works offline&#34; does not mean it has to satisfy a specific tick list. It's an idea, one that the makers of the web need to impress upon the world.</p>\n<h2>What does &#34;works offline&#34; mean?</h2>\n<p>I tried to spread the request for help via Reddit (a web site I very, very rarely visit) and one individual raised an interesting and valuable question (though it was phrased as a counter point): <em>isn't this just saving a cached copy?</em></p>\n<p>This is what we need to overcome with our software. For a site to work offline, is so much more, so much richer than the saved bones of an HTML page.</p>\n<p>The reality, today in fact, is that with the service worker capability we can deliver the same offline experience as many appstore installed mobile apps. At a fraction of the cost.</p>\n<h2>Is working offline the same as installable?</h2>\n<p>The short answer, as you know, is no. But installable isn't better than &#34;works offline&#34;. I've installed many applications from the app stores that I found out the hard way flat out didn't work without an internet connection (usually on my travels off of my home cellular network).</p>\n<p>Yet if I install software from the app store I expect it to work offline.</p>\n<p>If I visit a web site, I never expect it to work offline.</p>\n<p>What if you could tell me, when I visited your web site, that it worked offline.</p>\n<p>Absolutely yes, the browsers should provide badging. They <em>could</em> track if new entries were made to the origin's cache, and they could run a routed request for the URL I visited (stopping it from hitting the network layer preventing a double request if there wasn't middleware offline routing in place).</p>\n<p>Yet there's no indication that will come from browsers in the short term. So how about <a href=\"https://github.com/works-offline/logo/issues/1\">we do it ourselves</a>?</p>\n<p>The same way RSS went. How did you know a web site offered a feed of their content (before RSS was baked into browsersâ€¦or even after they all removed it)? Imagery, logos, word marks.</p>\n<p>RSS needed something obvious and clear that as a visitor I could subscribe. Dave Winer in 2005 (re?)started <a href=\"https://web.archive.org/web/20060221082210/http://www.reallysimplesyndication.com/2005/09/26#a970\">the conversation</a> and Microsoft eventually <a href=\"https://web.archive.org/web/20060227071704/http://blogs.msdn.com/rssteam/archive/2005/10/08/478505.aspx\">picked up the ball</a> (working with Mozilla if I read correctly) and that's how we <a href=\"https://web.archive.org/web/20051216113745/http://blogs.msdn.com/rssteam/archive/2005/12/14/503778.aspx\">got the RSS icon</a> (the original post is <a href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/archive/blogs/rssteam/icons-its-still-orange\">still live</a>, but missing the images).</p>\n<p>Slapping a bit of &#34;works offline&#34; on my site would be a great first step.</p>\n<h2>We need your help</h2>\n<p>What I'd personally like to see as an outcome: some simple iconography that I can use on my own site and other projects that can offer ambient badging to reassure my visitor that the URL they're visiting will work offline.</p>\n<p>Please, <a href=\"https://github.com/works-offline/logo/issues/1\">please contribute</a> if you can. There's already been some really wonderful work and this is a stage of trying anything and everything out.</p>\n<p>If, like me, <a href=\"https://www.brucelawson.co.uk/2020/no-to-service-worker-yes-to-wank/\">your skills don't lie in design</a>, then please help spread the word ðŸ™�</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2020/07/17/works-offline\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Adding BMPs to the Spectrum Next [til/spectrum]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/qTrpckTqkyE/adding-bmps-to-the-spectrum-next","description":"\n<p>The Spectrum Next has a dot command to load bitmaps, but there's a couple of tricks you need to pull off to be able to use it properly.</p>\n<h2>1. 8bit bitmap</h2>\n<p>First of all you'll need to get your image into an 8bit bitmap (.bmp files tend to come in the 24bit flavour).</p>\n<p>You can do this in Photoshop (here's <a href=\"https://medium.com/@chongfai13/convert-image-to-8bit-bmp-4634d732b218\">the directions</a>) or you can use <a href=\"https://online-converting.com/image/convert2bmp/\">online tools to convert</a> an image to a bitmap.</p>\n<p>The final image size wants to be 256x192.</p>\n<h2>2. Convert to Next friendly</h2>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://github.com/stefanbylund/zxnext_bmp_tools\">zxnext_bmp_tools</a> are needed. Windows users can download and use the .exe files, Mac and linux <a href=\"https://github.com/stefanbylund/zxnext_bmp_tools#how-to-build\">can compile</a> (it's a copy and paste job).</p>\n<p>I copied these to <code>~/bin/</code> and include that path in my <code>$PATH</code>. Then using the default <code>nextbmp</code> without options will convert the file ready for the Next (no output means success):</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-bash\">$ nextbmp myimage.bmp\n</code></pre>\n<h2>3. Using the image</h2>\n<p>I'm pretty sure the zxnext_bmp_tools output raw data that can be used, but in NextBASIC I'm using the dot command <code>.bmpload</code> as such:</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token number\">10</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>bmpload myimage<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>bmp\n<span class=\"token number\">20</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">PAUSE</span> <span class=\"token number\">0</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token comment\">; wait for a keypress</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>The one thing to be aware of after this point is that (as far as I gather) <code>.bmpload</code> is changing the palette (to be able to load the bitmap), so if you have tiles or sprites you want to show, you'll need to reset this before your own colours work.</p>\n<pre><code class=\"language-nextbasic\"><span class=\"token number\">10</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>bmpload myimage<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>bmp\n<span class=\"token number\">20</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">PAUSE</span> <span class=\"token number\">0</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span><span class=\"token comment\">; wait for a keypress</span>\n<span class=\"token number\">30</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">PALETTE</span> <span class=\"token keyword\">CLEAR</span>\n</code></pre>\n<p>Now everything after has the colours I expected.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til/spectrum/adding-bmps-to-the-spectrum-next\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=qTrpckTqkyE:cJiNJxRfmgY:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=qTrpckTqkyE:cJiNJxRfmgY:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/qTrpckTqkyE\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 08 Jun 2020 13:32:12 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=qTrpckTqkyE:cJiNJxRfmgY:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"8fc79d487df8d1995848666bc6401d4c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn19@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-36-598_ad7411de527866b2.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=qTrpckTqkyE:cJiNJxRfmgY:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn19@2020_2/2020/08/24/21-44-36-598_ad7411de527866b2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/qTrpckTqkyE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn11@2020_3/2020/08/24/21-44-57-311_8f4c200a07f90d38.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476255},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"Picking dependencies [blog]","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/remysharp/~3/ztJ25w9OPdU/picking-dependencies","description":"\n<p>Every web developer has faced this conundrum: which dependency should I pick? Why did we select jQuery over Prototype, or Prototype over Mootools, or Vue over React, or Angular over Ember, or Lodash over underscore and so on a forever for unlimited combinations for unlimited dependencies.</p>\n<p>My own process is internal and so fast that I'll often have arrived at my decision with what might appear as no thought. But this isn't so, and I thought it was about time I document some of my own process, least of all to allow myself to review it and adjust over time.</p>\n<h2>Types of dependency</h2>\n<p>When I'm looking for new dependencies I'm usually in one of two mindsets: looking for a framework level project or looking for a specific solution (a plugin, mini library, or the like). This also factors into what I consider important when I'm reviewing the options.</p>\n<p>What follows is a list that is generally in priority order when I'm considering a new dependency for my project.</p>\n<h2>1. Is the project actively maintained?</h2>\n<p>This is particularly important for smaller projects as they'll usually have a single individual working on the code. It's far from a deal breaker to visit an idle repository but I also need to consider the potential inherited technical dept from a new dependency.</p>\n<p>Two data points I'll look at are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Recency of commit activity - usually a scan over github's project landing page does the job here</li>\n<li>Age of any open pull requests - long held pull requests that have no activity on them might suggest the maintainer isn't around (I've certainly been this person with nodemon in the past).</li>\n</ul>\n<h2>2. Is the project used?</h2>\n<p>Popularity isn't a decider for me, but it does mean that the more the software is used, the more that bugs are found in the wild.</p>\n<p>In this case, I'm looking at:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Total issues</li>\n<li>Open issues - high open issues is not a negative factor</li>\n<li>Number of closed issues</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The speed in which the issues are closed, for me, isn't particularly important, particularly with a project that gets a lot of issues - what matters is that there's discussion going on.</p>\n<h2>3. Full depth of dependencies</h2>\n<p>In the land of Node and npm there's a running joke that the heaviest object in the universe, beyond the Sun, a neutron star and even beyond a black hole is: <code>node_modules</code>.</p>\n<p>This is a huge area of risk that somehow we web devs just take on the chin, thank goodness Deno is coming to the scene (Deno tries to solve by providing a stdlib which causes the dependency graph to stop spreading).</p>\n<p>So importantly this is not the count of dependencies (that you might see on sites like npmjs), but the full depth. Oddly I've only seen this available on <a href=\"http://Snyk.io\">Snyk.io</a> - ie. <a href=\"https://snyk.io/test/npm/nodemon?tab=dependencies\">nodemon's dependencies</a></p>\n<h2>4. Supply of live examples</h2>\n<p>Relevant to client side libraries, I want to see working interactive examples of the code running and be able to see enough of the code to recreate the demo myself.</p>\n<p>This offers immediate insight into answering the question: <em>&#34;does this do what I want&#34;</em>.</p>\n<h2>5. Documentation and complexity</h2>\n<p>Secondary to actually seeing code is, for me, documentation. Smaller projects I would expect to see example code in the readme document. Larger projects I'd hope to find multiple pages dedicated to docs.</p>\n<p>When I look at documents I'm looking for the starting examples and specifically asking: <em>does this require some additional build tools?</em></p>\n<p>Many projects I've come across have assumptions in the documentation, and the level of those assumptions add to complexity, particularly if I'm not familiar with the systems the project is referring to.</p>\n<p>For example, for me personally, nearly every Python project I've come across assumes knowledge of how to install a dependency - which I fall into the category of not being able to.</p>\n<h2>6. Version numbers</h2>\n<p>If a project isn't using semver this tends to be a red flag as there's a good amount of information that can be ascertained from a version number.</p>\n<p>As a reminder, <a href=\"https://semver.org/\">semver</a> uses major versions as an indicator of a breaking change, minor versions as a feature change and patch versions as bug fixes.</p>\n<p>There's a grey area that lives around documentation and refactoring (when the API remains exactly the same, but the inner workings are different, you have to release, but this doesn't align to any semver change).</p>\n<p>However, a high major version suggests high frequency of breaking changes - possibly risk to my project maintenance.</p>\n<p>A high minor number (such as Snyk's command line tool, currently at 1.323.0) suggests <em>lots</em> of features, possible a new release per feature.</p>\n<p>A high patch suggests, to me, stability and running in maintenance mode.</p>\n<h2>7. Age</h2>\n<p>This would be ageism in &#34;real life&#34; but in software project age can tell some important stories.</p>\n<p>An &#34;old&#34; project shows potential maturity or might even be a potential early signs of abandonment. What is old? If Node is 11 years old (in 2020) then anything around the decade mark is pretty old.</p>\n<p>I'd generally avoid an extremely young project (months old).</p>\n<hr>\n<p>A lot of this advice goes a long way towards: should the dependencies be created and owned by the project I'm working on?</p>\n<p>This is a question I tend to always ask myself, and if the specific problem I'm trying to solve is distinct enough, I might even pull the code in, copy in the license and a citation for the source and have it as a completely frozen dependency.</p>\n<p>If you're a web developer are there any other things you look for in your own auditing process?</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/2020/05/20/picking-dependencies\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div gsub(/^ /, &#34;&#34;, $0); print d $0 }'\n+zxls:1&#62; hdfmonkey ls /Applications/cspect/app/cspect-next-2gb.img /devel/Screenshots\n+zxrmdir:4&#62; zxrm '/devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found'\n+zxrm:1&#62; local FILENAME='/devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found'\n+zxrm:2&#62; basename '/devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found'\n+zxrm:2&#62; [ '/devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found' '=' 'opening dir: Path not found' ']'\n+zxrm:5&#62; echo hdfmonkey rm /Applications/cspect/app/cspect-next-2gb.img '/devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found'\nhdfmonkey rm /Applications/cspect/app/cspect-next-2gb.img /devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found\n+zxrm:6&#62; hdfmonkey rm /Applications/cspect/app/cspect-next-2gb.img '/devel/Screenshots/opening dir: Path not found'\nDeletion failed: Path not found\n+zxrmdir:4&#62; break\n+zxrmdir:6&#62; set +x\n</code></pre>\n<p>So above, I can see the errors and how the commands are being interpreted.</p>\n<p><em>Originally published on <a href=\"https://remysharp.com/til/cli/debugging-shell-scripts\">Remy Sharp's b:log</a></em></p><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?a=HWXCds7RANw:hAgp7Pik4Mg:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=HWXCds7RANw:hAgp7Pik4Mg:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/HWXCds7RANw\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 27 May 2020 11:57:54 +0000","feedId":3792,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=HWXCds7RANw:hAgp7Pik4Mg:F7zBnMyn0Lo","linkMd5":"54061458267cabccc0ca58f0057d0532","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn96@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-37-252_eaffc62150a3d0b3.webp","destWidth":105,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1058,"destBytes":436,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/remysharp?i=HWXCds7RANw:hAgp7Pik4Mg:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn96@2020_6/2020/08/24/21-44-37-252_eaffc62150a3d0b3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/remysharp/~4/HWXCds7RANw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn43@2020_4/2020/08/24/21-44-57-310_b61739184883b54c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598305476259},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 05:44:36","title":"How is \"nodemon\" pronounced?
